09-R-227
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT, WILLIAM M. BEAVERS,
JERRY BUTLER, JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN,
GREGG GOSLIN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND ROBERT B. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
WHEREAS, the Chief Financial Officer is responsible for the Bureau of Finance, as well as the
management oversight for the Comptroller, Budget, Revenue, Risk Management, Purchasing and
Contract Compliance Departments; and

1353

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, it is imperative to the successful operation of County government that the duties of the
Chief Financial Officer be carried out in an efficient and transparent manner; and
WHEREAS, in the case of a vacancy in the position of Chief Financial Officer, it is necessary to appoint
an Acting or Interim Chief Financial Officer to perform the duties of the Chief Financial Officer and said
Acting or Interim Chief Financial Officer shall have the full authority to otherwise execute the duties and
responsibilities of the Chief Financial Officer until a permanent Chief Financial Officer can be appointed
and approved; and
WHEREAS, due to a vacancy in the position of Cook County Chief Financial Officer, President Todd H.
Stroger appointed Joseph M. Fratto to serve as the Interim Chief Financial Officer; and
WHEREAS, due to his experience as Chief of Staff and his previous appointment as the Cook County
Comptroller, Joseph M. Fratto is highly knowledgeable of the County’s finances and the Finance Bureau
operation; he is highly qualified to manage the operations of the Bureau of Finance and perform the duties
of Interim Chief Financial Officer; and
WHEREAS, in addition to Joseph M. Fratto’s County experience, Mr. Fratto has over twenty-five years
experience in financial administration with the Chicago Park District and the Park Employee’s Annuity
and Benefit Fund, serving in a number of key positions within those organizations including Trustee and
Executive Director of the Benefit Fund, Deputy Superintendent of Finance and Management Services,
Superintendent of Finance and Administrative Services and Comptroller for the Park District; and
WHEREAS, in addition to his extensive finance experience, Mr. Fratto has a B.S. in Accounting and is a
licensed C.P.A.; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Fratto’s education, experience in financial administration and background in public
finance are an asset to Cook County and the Cook County Bureau of Finance.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois,
that the Board of Commissioners hereby approves the appointment of Joseph M. Fratto as Interim Chief
Financial Officer and grants Mr. Fratto the full authority to fulfill the responsibilities of Chief Financial
Officer and execute the duties of the Chief Financial Officer until a permanent candidate for Chief
Financial Officer can be appointed by the President and approved by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
In accordance with Cook County Code Section 2-108(z)(1) Amendment or suspension of rules,
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved to suspend Section 2-105(k)
Confirmation of Presidential appointments. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Murphy, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT, WILLIAM M. BEAVERS,
JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,

ANTHONY J. PERAICA, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER, PETER N. SILVESTRI,
DEBORAH SIMS, ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
RECOGNIZING MAY AS ASIAN PACIFIC ISLANDER AMERICAN HERITAGE MONTH
WHEREAS, Cook County is a diverse community of more than five million people with ancestries from
all parts of the world; and
WHEREAS, the more than 300,000 Asian-American residents of Cook County have contributed
significantly to the development of our neighborhoods and cities; and
WHEREAS, Asians, along with Irish immigrants and African-Americans among others, constructed and
operated the transcontinental railroads that passed through Cook County and provided the basis for our
county’s economic strength as a transportation center; and
WHEREAS, Cook County is home to Asian-American veterans who fought heroically for our nation
through many of her conflicts in the 20th century, including Filipinos who, alongside soldiers from
Maywood, Illinois, survived the Bataan Death March in the Philippines during World War II, and
Japanese Americans of the 100th Infantry Battalion and the 442nd Regimental Combat Teams who served
our nation with the highest military honors despite being designated for internment in American
concentration camps on the west coast; and
WHEREAS, Asian-American immigrants have made--and continued to make--tremendous efforts in
professional fields such as medicine, engineering, education, accounting and chemistry; and
WHEREAS, Asian-Americans, both native born and naturalized immigrants, are making strides in a
wider range of professional fields including government, the arts, journalism, the legal profession,
athletics, international trade, higher learning and the entertainment industry; and
WHEREAS, Asian-Americans are among the ranks of elected and appointed officials at the state and
national level, and are helping to shape the future of our nation and society, including: U.S. Secretary of
Veterans Affairs Eric Shinseki; U.S. Secretary of Commerce Gary Locke; U.S. Secretary of Energy
Steven Chu; former U.S. Secretary of Transportation Norman Mineta; U.S. Senators Daniel Inouye and
Daniel Akaka of Hawaii; Congresspersons Doris Matsui and Mike Honda (California); Mazie Hirono
(Hawaii); David Wu (Oregon); Bobby Scott (Virginia); Anh “Joseph” Cao (Louisiana); Eni
Faleomavaega (American Samoa); Gregorio “Kilili” Camacho Sablan (Northern Mariana Islanders); and
Louisiana Governor Bobby Jindal; California State Controller John Chiang; former Governor Benjamin
Cayetano of Hawaii; and

1355

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, Asian-Americans are among the ranks of both elected and appointed officials at the local
level including Cook County Judges Lynne Kawamoto, Sandra Otaka, Rena Van Tine, Sanjay Taylor,
Israel Desierto, Maria Kuriakos Ciesil, Neera Walsh, Skokie Park District Commissioner Jerry Clarito
and former Lincolnwood Mayor Peter Moy; and
WHEREAS, the Honorable Joseph Tecson, former Cook County Board Commissioner, served as the
first Asian-American Cook County Commissioner from 1977-1982; and
WHEREAS, Asian-Americans are in key positions in the news and entertainment industries such as
Yahoo! Founder Jerry Yang; Hollywood movie makers such as Brokeback Mountain’s Ang Lee, Mission
Impossible 2’s John Woo and Lady in the Water’s M. Night Shyamalan; authors Deepak Chopra and Amy
Tan; Cellist Yo Yo Ma; actors Keanu Reeves, Tamlyn Tomita, George Takei; recording artists Lea
Salonga, Ne-Yo, High School Musical’s Vanessa Hudgens, Smashing Pumpkins’ James Iha, Black Eyed
Peas’ Apl.de.ap; former NBC Entertainment President Scott Sassa; the Today show’s Ann Curry; CBS’
Early Show host Julie Chen; CNN medical reporter Dr. Sanjay Gupta; Lisa Ling; local television
personalities Joanie Lum, Linda Yu, Ellie Pai Hong, Nancy Loo, Mai Martinez, Jan Jeffcoat and Judy
Hsu; and Chicago White Sox and Chicago Blackhawks public address announcer Gene Honda; and
WHEREAS, Asian-Americans are a major force in various business and education sectors including:
fashion designer Vera Wang; TLC Beatrice Chief Executive Officer Loida Lewis; Avon Chief Executive
Officer Andrea Jung; AIDS /HIV researcher Dr. David Ho; designer of the Vietnam and Martin Luther
King, Jr. Memorials Maya Lin; internationally-renowned architect I.M. Pei; University of California at
Berkeley Chancellor Chang-Lin Tien; Wang Laboratories founder An Wang; Hotmail co-founder Sabeer
Bhatia; and
WHEREAS, Asian-American athletes, and Asians athletes in America are excelling individually and are
leading national sports teams and American professional sports teams to Olympic medals and world
championships including: WBC International Super Featherweight Champion Manny “Pacman”
Pacquiao; figure skater Michelle Kwan; short track speed skater Apolo Ohno; baseball players including
Kosuke Fukudome, Daisuke Matsusaka, Hideki Matsui, Ichiro Suzuki and Chien-Ming Wang; basketball
player Yao Ming; Pittsburgh Steelers wide receiver Hines Ward; the Major League Baseball Oakland A’s
Manager Don Wakamatsu; the National Basketball Association’s Miami Heat Coach Eric Spoelstra;
Tennessee Titans Offensive Coordinator Norman Chow; hockey player Paul Kariya; and professional
golfers Tiger Woods, Se Ri Pak and Michele Wie; and
WHEREAS, Cook County, primarily in departments under the Office of the President, employs the
largest number and percentage of Asian-Americans in any governmental workforce in Illinois, including
two department heads: Matthew DeLeon, the first Asian-American ever to serve as Secretary to the Board
of Commissioners and Takashi Reinbold, the first Asian-American to serve as Budget Director; and
WHEREAS, Asian-American Heritage Month provides Cook County an opportunity to restate its firm
stand against any and all discrimination on the basis of race, creed or national origin in Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners declare the
month of May as Asian-American Heritage Month in Cook County, and urge all residents and groups to
participate in the events sponsored by Asian-American organizations throughout the month of May.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION

THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER

PETER N. SILVESTRI, ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
HONORING THE LIFE OF ARTURO VELÁSQUEZ
WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called Arturo Velásquez from our midst and into
eternal life. Mr. Velásquez, a pillar of the Mexican community, provided assistance and leadership to the
Mexican and Latino community in an effort to level the American field of dreams and provide every
Latino an opportunity to succeed in the pursuit of happiness; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Velásquez was born in Tototlan, Jalisco in Mexico in 1915 and emigrated with his
parents to Gary, Indiana at the age of 8; Mr. Velásquez’ father, who owned a business in Mexico, soon
returned to Mexico; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Velásquez and his mother, who remained in Gary, Indiana, suffered through the
depression. Due to a lack of food, Mr. Velásquez and his mother attempted to return to Mexico; however,
a road accident in New Mexico prevented the Velásquez family from reaching their native Mexico.
Broke and stranded, Mr. Velásquez’ mother became a farm worker and migrated between sugar beet
fields in South Dakota and tomato farms in Minnesota and Iowa before finally settling in Chicago; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Velásquez attended thirteen grammar schools throughout his mother’s migration
through the sugar beet and tomato fields, and finally graduated from Haines Elementary School in
Chicago; and
WHEREAS, in 1936, Mr. Velásquez wedded Shirley Lozano, his loving wife of 72 years; together, Mr.
and Mrs. Velásquez raised 4 children: Arthur Raymond, President of Azteca Foods, Inc.; Carmen, Chief
Executive Officer of the Alivio Medical Center, a system of neighborhood clinics which, like Stroger
Hospital of Cook County, provides medical services to the poor; and Maria Elena and Edward who run
the family business; and

1357

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, in 1938, Mr. Velásquez founded the family business, Velásquez Automatic Music
Company, in the Back of the Yards neighborhood; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Velásquez was an Army Veteran having served the United States in World War II; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Velásquez was also instrumental in founding many civic and political organizations
including, but not limited to, the Azteca Lions Clubs, the Mexican American Chamber of Commerce, the
Illinois Federation of Mexican-Americans, the Spanish Speaking Study Commission, the Mexican Civic
Society, and the Mexican-American Democrats of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Velásquez was also an organizer and fundraiser for many local organizations including,
but not limited to, Holy Cross Church, the Cordi Marian Settlement Home, Holy Trinity High School, the
City Colleges Latino Scholarships, the Claretian Missionaries, the Ninos y Jovenes Orphanage in Jalisco,
Mexico, and the Alivio Medical Center; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Velásquez also gave back to his community through service as a trustee of National
Louis University and the City Colleges of Chicago; and
WHEREAS, on March 6, 2008, in recognition of Mr. Velásquez’ many contributions to the Mexican and
Latino community, and to the greater Chicago community, Mayor Richard M. Daley rededicated and
renamed West Side Technical Institute as the Arturo Velásquez West Side Technical Institute; and
WHEREAS, in 1999, Arturo Velásquez was also given the “El Reconocimiento OHTL” award from the
Mexican government – the highest award given by the Mexican government to a Mexican living outside
of Mexico; and
WHEREAS, the most thorough and most voluminous resolution or writing depicting the life of Mr.
Velásquez could never truly express or reflect the vastness and breadth of Mr. Velásquez’ commitment to
the Mexican and Latino community and his generosity to those less fortunate; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Velásquez is survived by his wife Shirley, his 4 children, 11 grandchildren, 19 greatgrandchildren, and his siblings, Marina, Eliseo, Josefina, and Elisia.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that Arturo
Velásquez’ memory shall be cherished in all of the hearts of the people he touched and loved; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf of more than
the 5 million residents of Cook County, on Tuesday, May 5, 2009, does hereby express its deepest
condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to Mr. Velásquez’ family as well as to the many friends and
loved ones of Mr. Arturo Velásquez, and may a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered herewith.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

09-R-230
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE WILLIAM M. BEAVERS, JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL,
JOHN P. DALEY, BRIDGET GAINER, ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN,
GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, on May 3, 1791 the Parliament of the Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth ratified a
democratic constitution; this democratic constitution was the first in Europe, and the second in the world,
after that of the United States of America, which was adopted in 1788; and
WHEREAS, the constitution of the Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth allowed for political equality
between townspeople and nobility, and placed the peasants under the protection of the government,
thereby tempering the worst abuses of serfdom; and
WHEREAS, King Stanislaw August Poniatowski described the May 3, 1791 Constitution as “founded
principally on those of England and the United States of America, but avoiding the faults and errors of
both, and adapted as much as possible to the local and particular circumstances of the country”; and
WHEREAS, the May 3, 1791 Constitution reflects Enlightenment influences, in particularly the
separation and balance of powers so that, in the language of Article V, “the integrity of the states, civil
liberty and social order remain always in equilibrium”; and
WHEREAS, Chicago hosts the largest Constitution Day Parade outside of Poland, and the Polish
American community in Cook County contributes substantially to the vibrancy of the culture and
economy of Cook County.

1359

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that I, Todd H. Stroger, President of the Cook County
Board of Commissioners, on behalf of the more than five million residents of Cook County, do hereby
declare May 3, 2009 as “Polish Constitution Day” in Cook County, and exhort all of our residents to be
cognizant of this great historical achievement.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

notice to public; agendas. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His Infinite Wisdom has called The Honorable Tyrone Kenner from our
midst; and
WHEREAS, Alderman Kenner was devoted to the City of Chicago and sought through political and
governmental means to improve the quality of life of its residents; and
WHEREAS, after serving honorably in the United States Air force, Alderman Kenner worked as a
boxing promoter, and then served as a Chicago police officer; and
WHEREAS, Alderman Kenner next held the position of Director of the Urban Progress Center, and later
became the Deputy Director of the Chicago Committee on Urban Opportunity; and

1360

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, Alderman Kenner was elected to the Chicago City Council in 1971 and served for thirteen
years; he was committed to rebuilding his ward; one of his greatest achievements was the refurbishing of
the 47th Street stop on the elevated line; and
WHEREAS, Alderman Kenner moved into the Robert Taylor Homes to draw attention to its poor living
conditions; he was also instrumental in facilitating the placement of a Chicago Police Department in the
Robert Taylor Homes to fight its increasing crime rate; and
WHEREAS, in losing Alderman Kenner we have lost a public servant who was loyal to the residents of
his ward and was a compassionate advocate on behalf of the poor.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that Alderman Tyrone Kenner’s memory shall be cherished
in all of the hearts of the people he touched and loved; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf of the more
than five million residents of Cook County, does hereby express its deepest condolences and most
heartfelt sympathy to the family as well as to the many friends and loved ones of Alderman Tyrone
Kenner, and may a copy of this Resolution be tendered herewith.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President

PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENTS
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
GREGG GOSLIN, PETER N. SILVESTRI, FORREST CLAYPOOL,
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, BRIDGET GAINER, JOHN P. DALEY,
ANTHONY J. PERAICA and LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
AMENDS COUNTY ORDINANCE PERTAINING TO ELECTION OF PRESIDENT
BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that Chapter 2 Administration,
Article II President of the County Board, Section 2-41, of the Cook County Code is hereby amended as
follows:
WHEREAS, most counties in Illinois are governed by the Executive Model of government whereby the
county executive serves as the chief executive officer of the county while the council or legislature serves
as the county's legislative body; and
WHEREAS, the Executive Model of government is common not just among counties but governments
throughout Illinois including the City of Chicago and Illinois state government; and
WHEREAS, it has been stated that the quality of local democracy will be enhanced by the introduction
of a separation of powers; and
WHEREAS, most forms of government do not allow their President or Chief Executive Officer to serve
a dual rule as a legislator/commissioner; and
WHEREAS, Cook County is unique in that the Illinois Constitution, Article 7, Section 4, subsection (b)
allows only Cook County to determine, by ordinance, that the chief executive officer can also serve as a
commissioner on the board which they govern; and
WHEREAS, it would better serve the residents of Cook County to have a separation of power between
the executive and legislative branches.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that to be consistent and fair to all residents of Cook
County, the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby amend the Cook County Code, Chapter 2
Administration, Article II President of the County Board, Section 2-41, to read as follows:

1362

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
(a) Election. The President of the Cook County Board shall be elected from the County at large and shall
be the Chief Executive Officer of the County. A person seeking election as President of the County Board
may NOT simultaneously seek election as a member of the Board.
Effective Date: This Ordinance Amendment is effective immediately upon passage.
_________________________
Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Gorman, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment be referred to the Committee on Finance. Commissioner Moreno called for a Roll Call, the
vote of yeas and nays being as follows:

Nays:

Commissioners Beavers, Butler, Maldonado, Moreno, Murphy, Steele - 6.

Commissioners Collins, Gainer, Sims - 3.

and the Proposed Ordinance Amendment was referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No.
300302).

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
AMENDMENT TO THE COOK COUNTY TAXPAYERS' ASSURANCE ORDINANCE
BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that Chapter 34 Finance, Section 344 of the Cook County Code is hereby amended as follows:
Sec. 34-4. Investment of public funds.
(a)
This section shall be known and may be cited as the "Cook County Taxpayers' Interest
Assurance Ordinance".

1363

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
(b)
All elected and appointed public officials of Cook County are directed to invest public
funds in their possession or for which they are custodians in interest-bearing accounts, except where
prohibited by law or for which compelling economic reasons do not justify the use of an interest-bearing
account. If any public funds are not invested in an interest-bearing account, the elected or appointed
public official shall certify in writing to the Chief Financial Officer and the County Auditor the reason
that such funds have not been invested in an interest-bearing account. The Chief Financial Officer and the
County Auditor will forward to the President of the County Board who, in turn, will forward to the
Chairman of the Audit Committee the correspondence received from the elected or appointed officials
indicating why public funds have not been invested in an interest-bearing account. On an annual basis,
the Chief Financial Officer shall report to the Audit Committee a listing of all depository accounts
including the department number, department name, name of account, depository institution, account
number, account balance, average daily balance, authorized signers, interest rate and any explanation or
certification for any no interest-bearing accounts.
(c)
The County Auditor shall report to the County Board as part of an annual audit of the
accounts of each elected and appointed public official:
(1)

The nature and amount of all funds for which such certifications have been
received from elected or appointed public officials;

(2)

The rates of return received by elected and appointed public officials on invested
funds; and

(3)

The average daily balance in the interest-bearing account in order to provide a
benchmark against which to evaluate the rate of return the elected and appointed
officials are earning on the funds.

(d)
Any public funds in the possession or custody of an elected or appointed public official
may be invested in any financial institution approved from time to time by the County Board as a
depository of public funds. The minimum requirements for any financial institution to be an approved
depository for County funds shall include:
(1)

Minimum capital requirement of $10,000,000.00;

(2)

The institution must have been in operation for at least five two years;

(3)

Located in Cook County, and

(4)

Meet regulatory requirement of the Community Reinvestment Act and not
engage in predatory lending practices.

No elected or appointed public official shall open any new account in an approved depository without
reporting the opening of such account to the County Auditor and the Chief Financial Officer of the
County within seven days of the opening of such account.

1364

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
(e)
Any elected or appointed public official who invests any public funds in any approved
depository which are in excess of the insured limits of such depository shall require that such depository
provide at least 102 percent collateral or provide a surety bond in an amount of 102 percent on any funds
in excess of the insured limit of such depository, except as provided in Subsection (f) of this section.
(f)
The Cook County Treasurer is authorized to make use of the Illinois Public Treasurer's
Investment Pool (IPTIP), pursuant to 30 ILCS 235/2(e) (1992), on a limited basis facilitate wire transfer
of funds due and owing to Cook County payable by the State of Illinois. Such funds, as they become due
to Cook County, may be invested by the Cook County Treasurer in the IPTIP for a period of time not to
exceed ten calendar days. The collateral requirement on County funds invested by the County Treasurer
in the IPTIP shall not be less than 102 percent.
Whenever a public agency deposits any public funds in a financial institution, the public agency shall
enter into an agreement with the financial institution requiring any funds not insured by the Federal
Depository Insurance Corporation to be collateralized by securities, a letter of credit or mortgage backed
securities in an amount equal to at least 102 percent of the market value of that amount of funds deposited
exceeding the insurance limitation provided by the Federal Depository Insurance Corporation. The letter
of credit must be issued by a financial institution that is rated "A" or better by at least two of the
following rating agencies: Fitch, Moody's and Standard & Poor's. Mortgage backed securities used as
collateral must be guaranteed by the Federal Home Loan Bank system, the Federal Home Loan Mortgage
Corporation or the Federal National Mortgage Association.
(g)
Except as provided in Subsection (f) of this section, Cook County funds placed in the
IPTIP shall be invested in the same manner, in the same types of investments and subject to the same
limitations provided for the investment of funds in the State Treasury.
(h)
The Cook County Treasurer, the Chief Financial Officer of Cook County and the County
Comptroller are authorized to execute on behalf of Cook County, an "Application and Agreement to
Participate in the Illinois Public Treasurer's Investment Pool", the terms of which shall not be inconsistent
with this section.
(i)
As used in this section, the term "public funds" shall mean current operating funds,
special funds, interest and sinking funds, and funds of any kind or character belonging to or in the custody
of any elected or appointed public official. The County Board may supersede the provisions of this
section should the authorizing ordinance specify the permitted investments and with respect to similar
funds held in a fiduciary capacity pursuant to statute or specific ordinance.
_________________________
This item was WITHDRAWN at the request of the sponsor.

09-O-28
ORDINANCE
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE GREGG GOSLIN, LARRY SUFFREDIN, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY
AND PETER N. SILVESTRI, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
AMENDMENT TO COOK COUNTY RETAIL ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT INCENTIVES
BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that Chapter 74 Taxation, Article
XV, Sections 74-582 through 74-584, of the Cook County Code is hereby amended as follows:
Sec. 74-582.

Definitions.

TIF District means a tax increment fund allocation financing district created by an Illinois
Municipal Corporation under the Illinois law.
Sec. 74-583.

Establishment of the Cook County Economic Development Incentives.

(e)
Cook County shall match dollar for dollar any sales tax rebate up to 50% of the County's
share of sales tax on the same terms as any Illinois Municipal Corporation provides a business; provided
Cook County is satisfied that the projections and the terms of the Illinois Municipal Corporation that such
rebate will provide additional retail sales and will establish or maintain retail jobs in Cook County are
reasonable.

1366

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
(e)
Cook County shall match, 50% of the lesser of (1) the dollar amount of any retailers'
occupation tax and/or service occupation tax rebate on the same terms as an Illinois Municipal
Corporation provides a business or (2) the County’s share of retailers’ occupation tax revenue and/or
service occupation tax revenue generated by said business on the same terms as that Illinois Municipal
Corporation provides said business; provided Cook County is satisfied that the projections of the
Illinois Municipal Corporation that such rebate (1) will provide additional retail sales and/or will
establish or maintain retail jobs in Cook County are reasonable, or (2) will, in the opinion of the Cook
County Board, be in the best economic interest of the County. No rebate will be granted to a retailer
related to the Cook County Home Rule Use Tax, Code of Ordinances of Cook County, Illinois 74-270 - 74281.
(f)
Cook County shall discourage relocation of business from one municipality to another
by requiring applicants to provide proof of increased sales tax revenues and the increase of jobs in
Cook County.

(f)
A business that is unable to create additional jobs and/or generate additional retail
sales may still apply to the Department of Planning and Development for a tax rebate. Any business
that applies for a rebate and is unable to create additional jobs and/or generate additional retail sales
must, as part of its application, establish that it is operated on a full time basis, current on all Cook
County taxes and fees, and is compliant with all labor laws, including prevailing wages. Each
application shall be considered on an individual basis, and the Department of Planning and
Development shall consider a number of factors, including but not limited to the applicant’s economic
impact study, economic hardship, business viability, the number of jobs the business shall maintain in
Cook County, and the amount of tax revenue that the business provides to the Illinois Municipal
Corporation at issue. As part of its application for a rebate, a business that is unable to create
additional jobs and/or generate additional retail sales shall present evidence to the Department of
Planning and Development that but for the rebate, the retailer will be forced to move its business out
of Cook County. As part of its application, the business must establish that any tax rebate it receives
from Cook County will be used for capital improvements, fixed asset improvements, statutory or other
business development expenses, and not as profit. The Department of Planning and Development shall
develop further criteria for evaluation of any such application. After reviewing a business’s
application, the Department of Planning and Development transmit its
recommendation to the
President, and the matter shall be presented to the Cook County Board for approval.
(g)
Cook County shall terminate an agreement with the Illinois Municipal Corporation
and applicant if the Department of Planning and Development regulations are not adhered to.
(g)
In order for a business that is unable to create additional jobs and/or generate
additional retail sales to be eligible for a tax rebate, the business shall maintain not less than both (1)
250 full time employees, and (2) $50 Million in retail sales per year.
(h)
Cook County shall discourage relocation of a business from one municipality to
another by requiring applicants to provide proof of increased sales tax revenues and the increase of
jobs in Cook County. Should any business that has received a tax rebate from Cook County
subsequently move out of Cook County, the business shall pay Cook County one hundred percent
(100%) of any tax revenues rebated to the business during the five (5) years prior to the year the
business moved out of Cook County.

1367

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
(i)
Cook County shall terminate an agreement with the Illinois Municipal Corporation and
applicant if the Department of Planning and Development regulations are not adhered to or if the
Department of Planning and Development determines that any information provided in a business’s
application for a tax rebate is false, incomplete or inaccurate.
(j)
With respect to an applications made pursuant to the provisions of subsections 74-583
(f) and (g) herein above, the Cook County Board will not approve such application, and will terminate
any such application which has been approved, in the event real property utilized in the retail business
regarding which the application was made, is or has been designated Class 8a pursuant to Cook
County Ordinance 09-O-26 approved and adopted April 15, 2009.
Sec. 74-584

County Option to Terminate.

Any application approved by the Cook County Board under the provisions of this Ordinance is
subject to termination by the Cook County Board in the event, and as of the effective date, of a change
in the Cook County rate of the retailers’ occupation tax and/or the service occupation tax which was in
effect at the time such application was approved.
Effective date: This Ordinance Amendment shall be effective upon adoption.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

HOME RULE COUNTY RETAILERS’ OCCUPATION TAX
BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that Chapter 74 Taxation, Article IV,
Sections 74-150 through 74-152, of the Cook County Code are hereby amended as follows:
ARTICLE IV. RETAILERS’ OCCUPATION TAX.
Sec. 74-150.

Short title.

This article shall be known and may be cited as the Cook County Home Rule County Retail
Occupation Tax Ordinance.
Sec. 74-151.

Imposed.

As authorized by 55 ILCS 5/5-1006 (home rule county retailers' occupation tax law), a tax is
imposed Countywide upon all persons in the County engaged in the business of selling tangible personal
property at retail, at the rate of one and three-quarters percent (1.75%) one and one quarter percent
(1.25%) for the period of three-quarters percent (.75%) effective January 1, 2010 to December 31, 2010;
and three-quarters percent (.75%) thereafter, of the gross receipts from such sales made in the course of
such business. The tax shall be paid in the manner provided in such statute.
Sec. 74-152.

Notification of the Illinois Department of Revenue.

The Clerk of the Board is hereby authorized and directed to obtain and transmit a certified copy
of this Ordinance to the Illinois Department of Revenue not later than five days after its effective date,
and in no case later than April October 1, 2008 2009 so as to enable the Illinois Department of Revenue to
proceed to administer and enforce this Ordinance, on behalf of the County of Cook, as of July January 1,
2008 2010.

1369

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
Effective date: This Ordinance shall take effect upon passage, except that the rate decreases in Section
74-151 shall not take effect until January 1, 2010.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.

09-O-30
ORDINANCE
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, JOHN P. DALEY,
GREGG GOSLIN, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER

HOME RULE COUNTY SERVICE OCCUPATION TAX
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that Chapter
74 Taxation, Article V, Sections 74-190 through 74-192, of the Cook County Code are hereby amended
as follows:
ARTICLE V. SERVICE OCCUPATION TAX.
Sec. 74-190.

Short title.

This article shall be known and may be cited as the Cook County Home Rule County Service
Occupation Tax Ordinance.
Sec. 74-191.

Imposed.

As authorized by 55 ILCS 5/5-1007 (home rule county service occupation tax law), a tax is
imposed Countywide upon all persons in the County engaged in the business of selling tangible personal
property at retail, at the rate of one and three-quarters percent (1.75%) one and one quarter percent
(1.25%) for the period of three-quarters percent (.75%) effective January 1, 2010 to December 31, 2010;
and three-quarters percent (.75%) thereafter, of the gross receipts from such sales made in the course of
such business. The tax shall be paid in the manner provided in such statute.
Sec. 74-192.

Notification of the Illinois Department of Revenue.

The Clerk of the Board is hereby authorized and directed to obtain and transmit a certified copy
of this Ordinance to the Illinois Department of Revenue not later than five days after its effective date,
and in no case later than April October 1, 2008 2009 so as to enable the Illinois Department of Revenue to
proceed to administer and enforce this Ordinance, on behalf of the County of Cook, as of July January 1,
2008 2010.
Effective date: This Ordinance shall take effect upon passage, except that the rate decreases in Section
74-191 shall not take effect until January 1, 2010.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

PROPOSED RESOLUTIONS
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
EARLEAN COLLINS, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
REVIEW OF FEDERAL STIMULUS DOLLARS FOR
COOK COUNTY’S UNEMPLOYED ADULTS, DISLOCATED WORKERS AND YOUTH
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII, Section 6 (a)
of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exercise any power and perform any function
pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the President’s Office of Employment Training (“P.O.E.T”) along with the Cook County
Workforce Investment Board (“WIB”) are committed to assisting the residents of suburban Cook County
through the administration of the federally supported Workforce Investment Act (“WIA”) program which
provides residents with employment training, job placement, and educational opportunities; and
WHEREAS, statistics show that long term unemployed individuals are more likely to turn to crime and
with unemployment rates in Cook County above the national average it is paramount that P.O.E.T. along
with the Workforce Investment Board utilize the 15.5 million dollars from the Federal Economic
Stimulus Package dollars effectively.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that this Board conduct a public hearing to discuss the
allocation of 15.5 million dollars for Cook County’s unemployed adults, dislocated workers and youth.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ROBERTO MALDONADO, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO and PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, on April 9, 2009 the Cook County Health & Hospitals System Board (“System Board”)
adopted the Procurement Policy for the Cook County Health & Hospitals System (“System”); and
WHEREAS, the System Board took this action pursuant to the Ordinance Establishing the Cook County
Health & Hospitals System (“Enabling Ordinance”) which expressly provides that the System Board shall
have the authority over all procurement and contracts for the System, and further provides that the System
may exercise this authority, in whole or in part, pursuant to its discretion; and
WHEREAS, as the System’s Interim Chief Executive Officer (“CEO”), David R. Small, stated in a letter
to the Board of Commissioners dated April 20, 2009, the System Board has stated that it is genuinely
committed to the County’s policy to promote equal opportunity in its procurement process and has
expressly set forth in the System’s new Procurement Policy that Protected Class Enterprises shall
participate in not less than 35 percent of the annual aggregate value of all contracts awarded by the
System; and
WHEREAS, in furtherance of its mission to ensure sound fiscal management of all aspects of the
System, the System has issued a Request for Proposal (“RFP”) for the System’s participation in a Group
Purchasing Organization (“GPO”), a purchasing consortia that the Systems argues is in the best interest of
the System and its patients; and
WHEREAS, numerous local small business owners who are certified as Minority and Women Owned
Business Enterprises (“M/WBEs”) oppose the System’s use of a GPO stating that it would eliminate their
ability to do business with the County because GPOs shut out small M/WBE businesses and offer
opportunities only to majority corporations who pay to participate in GPO contracts; and
WHEREAS, as an example of this exclusion, the M/WBE business owners allege that a vendor currently
supplying pharmaceuticals to the System through a contract previously approved by the County Board
has not met its M/WBE participation goals as agreed to in its contract; and
WHEREAS, the System disputes this allegation, stating that the County Board approved a reduced
M/WBE participation goal of 3 percent due to the stringent manufacture and delivery standards for the
purchase of pharmaceuticals and the vendor is satisfying this participation; and
WHEREAS, the Director of the Office of Contract Compliance states a different finding in a
Memorandum to the Chair of Contract Compliance, dated April 20, 2009, concluding that the
pharmaceutical vendor’s 3% goal has not been met.

1376

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that in an effort to protect the integrity of the M/WBE
Ordinance and the impact utilization of GPOs will have on M/WBEs, the Contract Compliance
Committee of the Cook County Board will convene a public hearing and will request to hear testimony
from the following: Warren Batts, Chairman, System Board; David R. Small, Interim System CEO;
Leslie Duffy, System Chief Procurement Officer; Betty Hancock Perry, Director of the Office of Contract
Compliance; and representatives from the M/WBE small business community, as well as from other
members of the public.
_________________________
In accordance with Cook County Code Section 2-108(z)(1) Amendment or suspension of rules,
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved to suspend Section 2-108(h)(1) Prior
notice to public; agendas. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Contract Compliance. (Comm. No. 300319). The motion carried
unanimously.
RESOLUTIONS
09-R-232
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOSEPH MARIO MORENO AND JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN P. DALEY, BRIDGET GAINER, ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY
GORMAN, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS AND ROBERTO MALDONADO
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
REQUESTING A NO-COST PILOT PROGRAM FOR
REVERSE AUCTION E-PROCUREMENT SOLUTION
WHEREAS, the FY2009 budget process again saw substantial cuts, with an across-the-board 4% budget
cut for all departments and elected officials with the exception of court ordered programs, and a 2% cut
for the Cook County Health & Hospitals System; and
WHEREAS, Cook County government must continue to undertake serious efforts to create efficiencies
in the delivery of its services, not solely because of the current difficult economic situation the country is
faced with, but because it is the duty of this Honorable Body to ensure that taxpayers’ money is invested
wisely and that this government is doing everything in its power to continually identify cost savings and
streamlining opportunities in order to deliver quality services in the most efficient and cost effective
manner possible; and

1377

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, online reverse auctions have been successfully used in the private sector procurement
process for over a decade; and
WHEREAS, reverse auctions have evolved to be able to meet the public sector procurement
requirements, which leads to increased savings, more efficient operations and decreased expenditures; and
WHEREAS, in addition to the increased savings, online reverse bidding solutions enable a transparent
process capable of being monitored in real-time; creates increased competition; improves vendor
participation; reduces procurement time cycle and government administrative costs; creates an audit trail
and reporting efficiencies; and creates a disaster recovery archive; and
WHEREAS, online reverse auction providers can deliver a real-time, secure, web-based electronic
bidding process with all of the above mentioned benefits all at no cost to the governmental entity, with
fees being paid by the successful bidder; and
WHEREAS, the State of Illinois is now considering using said bidding solution to streamline its
procurement process, with the passing of House Bill 379, which has now moved to the Senate for further
consideration; and
WHEREAS, the City of Chicago has already completed a similar pilot program and is currently seeking
to expand the service, allowing all City of Chicago Departments to participate, with the same goal of
streamlining its procurement process and saving taxpayer dollars.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, does
hereby request that the Purchasing Department conduct a no-cost to the County pilot program for a
reverse auction e-procurement solution with the goal of qualifying and quantifying the efficiencies
created using this procurement solution and the accompanying savings; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the pilot program should have a duration of 12 months and include
no less than six procurements using the online reverse auction solution with three of the six procurements
consisting of one each of the following categories: services, commodities and construction.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried.
Commissioner Butler voted "no".

09-R-233
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, PETER N. SILVESTRI,
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN AND JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, JOHN P. DALEY, BRIDGET GAINER,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, DEBORAH SIMS AND ROBERT B. STEELE
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
REQUESTING THE INTEGRATION OF
ORGANIC ENHANCING PRODUCTS TO TREAT ROAD SALT
WHEREAS, the Cook County Highway Department has the responsibility of designing and maintaining
over 573 center line miles of highways, many of which, are part of the major arterial network that leads to
and from area expressways and toll roads, including two-lane highways, and has maintenance
responsibilities for 1,478 lane miles of pavement and 132 bridges, 351 traffic signals and 7 pumping
stations from five maintenance garages throughout Cook County; and
WHEREAS, snow removal, anti-icing and de-icing applied measures on all highways, bridges and roads
under the jurisdiction of Cook County are the responsibility of the Cook County Highway Department;
and
WHEREAS, de-icing is a reactive snow and ice control strategy that involves the application of a
chemical, most commonly road salt, on top of a layer of snow, ice, or frost that has already bonded to the
surface of the pavement; and
WHEREAS, anti-icing is a proactive strategy in which snow and ice control materials are applied before
a snow, ice or frost event, preventing precipitation from bonding with the pavement surface; and
WHEREAS, rates of application of road salt vary from 25 lbs to 400 lbs per lane mile with more road
salt per lane mile used the lower the actual temperature or forecasted temperature and the heavier
precipitation type; and
WHEREAS, up to 80 percent of untreated road salt is lost with traffic action to the roadside environment,
while pre-wetting or pre-treating the salt with liquid chemicals has proven to help the material “stick” to
the roadway; and
WHEREAS, the Median Cost per Ton of road salt has increased from $36 USD in 2003 to $120 USD in
2008 in the United States, with a final cost to Cook County during the 2008 winter of $125 per ton, a total
expense of four million dollars over the estimated budget for road salt; and

1379

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, according to the National Cooperative Highway Research Program (NCHRP) Report 577,
published in 2007 and sanctioned by the National Academy of Sciences, all snow and ice control
materials can affect the environment with roadway application being the primary source of runoff,
causing significant localized effects; and
WHEREAS, the same report states that Chloride-induced corrosion of reinforcing steel from the use of
road salt is the most widely occurring cause of concrete deterioration, posing the highest risk to structural
integrity because it causes a very localized attack on the steel, resulting in high cost for maintenance and
repairs. Chloride-induced corrosion is also the primary cause of bridge steel structural corrosion; and
WHEREAS, loss of capital related to corrosion damage from the snow and ice control chemicals on
water supplies, health, vegetation, highway structures, vehicles, and underground utilities exceed 15 times
the amount of money spent on purchasing and applying said chemicals; and
WHEREAS, according to the NCHRP report, snow and ice-control organic products used in conjunction
with road salt, have demonstrated significant corrosion inhibiting characteristics as well as increased
overall product performance; and
WHEREAS, the use of snow and ice-control organic enhancers in conjunction with road salt, has proven
to be a cost effective and environmentally friendly alternative to traditional snow and ice-control products
by improving the road salt performance, reducing overtime costs, preventing corrosion and reducing the
overall environmental impact; and
WHEREAS, several Counties in Illinois have seen at least 20% savings in their cost of road salt by
integrating organic enhancers, including Du Page County for the last two years, Lake County for the
last three years, McHenry County for the last seven years, Winnebago County for the last year, Jo Daviess
County for the last five years, Peoria County for the last two years, Henry County for the last four years
and Knox County for the last four years; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Highway Department currently does not use organic enhancers in
conjunction with road salt for snow and ice-control.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby request that the Highway Department start the process of integrating organic enhancing products
to treat road salt provided that said products lower the cost to Cook County for snow removal and icecontrol expenses related to road salt usage, and equipment and structural maintenance for FY 2009 and
future years.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

09-R-234
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
A RESOLUTION CONSENTING TO THE CREATION OF
SCHAUMBURG SPECIAL SERVICE AREA NUMBER 12,
AND THE INCLUSION OF A PROPERTY LOCATED
WITHIN UNINCORPORATED COOK COUNTY IN
SCHAUMBURG SPECIAL SERVICE AREA NUMBER 12
(MEADOW KNOLLS SUBDIVISION WATERMAIN - EAST)
WHEREAS, portions of the area commonly known as the Meadow Knolls Subdivision are not connected
to a public water supply, but rather have wells; said properties being legally described on Exhibit A, and
depicted on Exhibit B, both Exhibits being submitted herewith and made part hereof (hereinafter referred
to as the “SSA PROPERTIES”); and
WHEREAS, it is in the best interests of the SSA PROPERTIES to have access to a public water supply;
and
WHEREAS, the Village of Schaumburg (hereinafter referred to as the “VILLAGE”) has agreed to install
an extension to the VILLAGE’S water system to service the SSA PROPERTIES, provided said water
system can be constructed pursuant to a special service area to pay for the cost thereof (hereinafter
referred to as the “MEADOW KNOLLS EAST SSA”); and
WHEREAS, one (1) of the SSA PROPERTIES is located in unincorporated Cook County (hereinafter
referred to as the “COUNTY”), said property being legally described on Exhibit C, and depicted on
Exhibit D, both Exhibits being submitted herewith and made part hereof (hereinafter referred to as the
“UNINCORPORATED PARCEL”), with the remainder of the SSA PROPERTIES being located in the
VILLAGE and, as such, pursuant to 35 ILCS 200/27-5, the COUNTY must consent to the inclusion of
the UNINCORPORATED PARCEL in the MEADOW KNOLLS EAST SSA and the creation of the
MEADOW KNOLLS EAST SSA by the VILLAGE; and
WHEREAS, the VILLAGE has requested that the COUNTY consent to the inclusion of the
UNINCORPORATED PARCEL in the MEADOW KNOLLS EAST SSA, so that the owner of the
UNINCORPORATED PARCEL can have access to a public water supply; and
WHEREAS, the owner of the UNINCORPORATED PARCEL is aware of the request being made of the
COUNTY, and is in favor of the COUNTY granting said consent so that the owner of the
UNINCORPORATED PARCEL can have access to a public water supply; and
WHEREAS, it is necessary for the public health, safety and welfare that the MEADOW KNOLLS EAST
SSA be formed so that a public water supply can be provided to the SSA PROPERTIES, including the
UNINCORPORATED PARCEL; and
WHEREAS, the COUNTY concurs in the desire of the VILLAGE to provide a public water supply to
the SSA PROPERTIES, including the UNINCORPORATED PARCEL; and

1381

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, it is necessary to memorialize the COUNTY’S approval of the inclusion of the
UNINCORPORATED PARCEL in the MEADOW KNOLLS EAST SSA, and the COUNTY’S consent
to the creation of the MEADOW KNOLLS EAST SSA.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners, Cook
County, Illinois, as follows:
SECTION 1: That the COUNTY, pursuant to 35 ILCS 200/27-5, hereby gives its consent to the
creation of the MEADOW KNOLLS EAST SSA and to the VILLAGE’S inclusion of the
UNINCORPORATED PARCEL in the MEADOW KNOLLS EAST SSA.
SECTION 2: That the County Clerk is hereby directed to forward three (3) certified copies of
this Resolution to Marilyn J. Karr, Village Clerk, Village of Schaumburg, 101 Schaumburg Court,
Schaumburg, Illinois 60193.

approval as provided by law.

1382

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners approved Resolution 07-R-62 on January 23,
2007, extending military leave benefits to Cook County employees serving in the military reserve; and
WHEREAS, Resolution 07-R-62 expired on December 31, 2007; and
WHEREAS, the United States has continued to undertake military reserve operations after the terrorist
acts against the United States of America, in both the Afghanistan and Iraq theaters of operation, as well
as national interest endeavors worldwide; and
WHEREAS, employees of the County of Cook who are members of the military reserve force of the
United States or of the State of Illinois have been called to active duty which has caused an economic
hardship upon such employees and their families; and
WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Cook County Board to provide transitional assistance to such
employees and their families while they are adjusting to the changed set of circumstances.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners:
In addition to the paid fifteen-day leave of absence provided in the Cook County Code, Section
44-95 Military Leave, governing military leave and applicable collective bargaining agreements,
employees of Cook County who are members of the reserve force of the State of Illinois who have been
or are ordered to active duty by appropriate authorities shall be eligible for additional paid leave and
benefits, as provided for herein.
The Chairman of the Committee on Finance, the Chief of the Bureau of Human Resources, and
the President’s designated Chief Financial Officer, or their designees, shall constitute the Military
Benefits Committee. All rules previously adopted by the Committee shall remain in place unless modified
by the Committee. Paid leave shall be in amounts equal to the employee’s regular monthly salary minus
his/her military base pay compensation. Benefits to be continued for employees called to military duty
under this Ordinance shall include continuation of family medical coverage under the plan currently in
force for each employee. The Committee will approve or disapprove such applications based on the
application for additional paid leave and the applicant's employment information contained in Cook
County records. The Committee shall report to the Cook County Board of Commissioners each denial
of an application for additional paid leave within thirty days after the denial.
Additional paid leave hereunder shall automatically terminate upon the termination of active duty
in connection with active duty status.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Gorman, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

09-R-237
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT
AND JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE WILLIAM M. BEAVERS, JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL,
EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, BRIDGET GAINER,
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the holiday of Cinco de Mayo commemorates the victory of the Mexican militia over the
French army at The Battle of Puebla, Mexico, 100 miles east of Mexico City, on the morning of May 5,
1862; and
WHEREAS, lead by Mexican General Ignacio Zaragoza Seguin, a small, poorly armed militia estimated
at 4,500 men demonstrated their courage and sacrifice for freedom by stopping and defeating a well
outfitted French army of 6,500 soldiers, which had known no defeat for almost 50 years, therefore
postponing the invasion of the country for a full year; and

1385

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, this victory was a glorious moment for Mexican patriots, helping develop a needed sense of
national unity and pride; and
WHEREAS, according to a paper published by the UCLA Center for the Study of Latino Health and
Culture in 2007, about the origin of the observance of Cinco de Mayo in the United States, the modern
American focus on this holiday first started in California in 1863 in response to the resistance to French
rule in Mexico, and has since been celebrated continuously while virtually ignored in Mexico, where it is
celebrated mainly in the southern town of Puebla and a few larger cities, and has to this day not been
recognized as a federal holiday, and
WHEREAS, celebrating Cinco de Mayo has become increasingly popular in parts of the U.S. that have a
high population of Americans of Mexican ancestry, making of this holiday a celebration of Mexican
culture, food, music, beverage and customs unique to Mexico; and
WHEREAS, the cultural impact of the Cinco de Mayo holiday is evident in more than 150 official
celebrations in towns across the U.S. that are predominately non-Hispanic, and
WHEREAS, over 70% of Hispanics living in Cook County are of Mexican descent and make numerous
cultural and economic contributions to the growth and development of our county.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf
of the more than five million residents of Cook County, does hereby join in the celebration of Cinco de
Mayo, and encourage all Cook County residents to join in this celebration of the Mexican culture and
heritage; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

09-R-238
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
RESOLUTION URGING THE ILLINOIS GENERAL ASSEMBLY TO AMEND
CHAPTER 35 OF THE STATE STATUTES CONCERNING THE
DISTRIBUTION OF PROCEEDS FROM THE MOTOR FUEL TAX FUND
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, in Illinois, is the second largest county in the United States; and

1386

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, the most recent U.S. Census data from July 2008 estimates Cook County’s population at
5,294,664 or 43.3% of Illinois residents; and
WHEREAS, the latest FY2008 data from the Illinois Secretary of State indicates that Cook County has
3,490,693 registered vehicles or 2,590,316 more than the next closest county; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Highway Department was established in 1913 by the State of Illinois upon
approval of the first officially recorded County highway system maps; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Highway Department has the responsibility of designing and maintaining
over 573 center line miles of highways, many of which, are part of the major arterial network that leads to
and from area expressways and toll roads, including multi-lane highways, and has maintenance
responsibilities for 1,478 lane miles of pavement, 132 bridges, 351 traffic signals throughout Cook
County and seven pumping stations from five maintenance garages; and
WHEREAS, many municipalities of Cook County, including Chicago, have or will receive millions of
dollars in Federal Stimulus monies for road construction and maintenance projects; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Highway Department will only receive $213,000 in Federal Stimulus
money; and
WHEREAS, the County, therefore, must rely solely on the monies it receives from the State of Illinois
through the Motor Fuel Tax (MFT) receipts, which is almost exclusively the funding source for County
highway projects, and the local gas tax to maintain its roads and bridges; and
WHEREAS, Cook County’s share of the MFT fund, per State statute, is 16.74% due to its status as the
only County in Illinois with over 1,000,000 or more inhabitants; and
WHEREAS, in the coming years, several other Illinois counties may also reach the 1,000,000 inhabitant
milestone, and consequently Cook County’s share of the MFT fund could be substantially cut; and
WHEREAS, such a drastic reduction in the County of Cook’s MFT distribution would have an adverse
effect on the County Highway Department’s ability to fulfill its mission; and
WHEREAS, Cook County’s status as the most populous County by far, in Illinois, as well as having the
most registered vehicles and the most frequently used roads and bridges under its jurisdiction should be
recognized and consequently funded appropriately and reliably.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, does
hereby urge that the Illinois General Assembly, amend Chapter 35 ILCS 505/8 (e) (2) (B) as follows:
16.74% to the counties of the State having 1,000,000 3,000,000 or more inhabitants; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that by enacting said amendment the State of Illinois will ensure that
the Cook County Highway Department will have a reliable and steady funding source; and

1387

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this Honorable Body encourages the State of Illinois to increase its
funding of the Cook County Highway Department for the successful operation of its critical mission for
the foreseeable future.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION IN SUPPORT OF LIFTING DISCRIMINATORY SANCTIONS
AGAINST ITALIAN MINERAL WATER
WHEREAS, the United States Trade Representative had proposed a 100% import duty on mineral water
imported from the Republic of Italy; and
WHEREAS, these sanctions were the incidental result of an ongoing trade dispute between the United
States and the European Union (EU) on hormone beef; and
WHEREAS, the United States Trade Representative had modified the list of European import duties
which are authorized by the World Trade Organization (WTO); and
WHEREAS, no other mineral water imported to the United States was subject to the imposition of this
new import duty; and
WHEREAS, Italy currently produces 12% of the world’s mineral water, 40% which is exported to the
United States, which amounted to $58 million in exports to the United States; and
WHEREAS, the proposed imposition of this duty hurts businesses in Italy, a steadfast ally of our nation,
and in the Region of Emilia Romagna, our sister county in Italy; and

1388

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, sixty Italian restaurants in Chicago and suburban Cook County initiated a petition to the
United States Trade Representative, requesting that the discriminatory duty imposed be abolished.
NOW THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Cook County Board of
Commissioners stand in solidarity with the Italian-American community of Cook County, including the
sixty restaurants in our county initiating the petition, and the Italian-American Chamber of CommerceMidwest, in urging the United States Trade Representative to avoid this arbitrary and unfair
discriminatory duty against our sister county and the entire nation of Italy and negotiate a settlement with
the EU; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be forwarded to the President of the
United States, members of the delegation of the State of Illinois in the United States Congress, Senators
Richard Durbin and Roland Burris.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

09-R-241
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, in 1987 the National Stroke Association received a Presidential Proclamation to celebrate
“National Stroke Awareness Month” annually in May; and
WHEREAS, strokes occur when blood clots impede the flow of blood to the brain, thereby damaging the
brain; two-thirds of the people who experience a stroke are left with a disability; and
WHEREAS, stroke is the third leading cause of death in the United States; and
WHEREAS, there are a number of steps you can take to avoid experiencing a stroke; indeed eighty
percent of all strokes are preventable; and
WHEREAS, the following are treatable diseases/conditions/behaviors that increase stroke risk: high
blood pressure (hypertension), arterial fibrillation, high cholesterol, diabetes, smoking, excessive alcohol
use and excessive weight; and
WHEREAS, “transient ischemic attacks” are brief episodes of stroke-like symptoms that last from a few
minutes to twenty-four hours; while these attacks cause no damage, they are often serious warning signs
of an impending stroke; and

1390

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, it is important to be able to recognize when a person has just experienced a stroke, and to
get them immediate medical treatment; the acronym “FAST” stands for “Face” – Ask the person to smile;
does one side droop?/ “Arm” – Ask the person to lift both arms; does one arm drift downward?/”Speech”
– Ask the person to repeat a simple phrase; does the speech sound slurred or strange?/”Time” – If you
observe any of these signs, call 911.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that I, Todd H. Stroger, President of the Cook County
Board of Commissioners, on behalf of the more than five million residents of Cook County, do hereby
recognize May as “National Stroke Awareness Month” in Cook County, and do urge all residents to be
cognizant of the steps they can take to minimize their risk of experiencing a stroke as well as the steps
they can take to respond in a swift manner to another’s or their own stroke.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

09-R-243
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, as is customary, this year Mother’s Day is being celebrated on the second Sunday of May,
which is May 10th; and
WHEREAS, on Mother’s Day we recognize the positive and priceless contributions that mothers make to
society; and
WHEREAS, on Mother’s Day we express gratitude for the hardships mothers bear and the sacrifices
mothers make in raising children; and
WHEREAS, Mother’s Day first was celebrated in 1907 at Andrew’s Methodist Episcopal Church in
Grafton, West Virginia (now the International Mother’s Day Shrine and a National Historic Landmark),
where Ann Jarvis, who was crusading to found a national memorial day for women, handed out
carnations to all the mothers at church; the custom caught on and eventually spread to forty-six states; and
WHEREAS, on May 8, 1914, the U.S. Congress passed a law designating the second Sunday in May as
Mother’s Day and requested a proclamation from President Woodrow Wilson; on May 9, 1914, President
Wilson made that proclamation, declaring the first national Mother’s Day as a day for American citizens
to show the flag in honor of those mothers whose sons had died in war; and
WHEREAS, on Mother’s Day we celebrate the precious love and irreplaceable relationships we share
with our mothers.

1392

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that I, Todd H. Stroger, President of the Cook County
Board of Commissioners, on behalf of the more than five million residents of Cook County, do hereby
recognize Sunday, May 10, 2009 as Mother’s Day in Cook County, and do hereby urge all residents to
cherish and honor the bonds they share with their mothers.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.

approximately seventeen years ago; he was holding a sign that read, “Homeless. Work for Food. God
Bless”; this experience galvanized her, and after a year of organizing, she was instrumental in creating the
Southwest Chicago Public Action to Deliver Shelter (PADS) in 1993; and
WHEREAS, PADS is an ecumenical and community venture which values the dignity, uniqueness,
goodness and giftedness of all persons; PADS both seeks to stem homelessness by providing immediate
assistance and referrals to those facing a housing crisis, and to assist the homeless in becoming ready for
and procuring stable employment and housing; and
WHEREAS, Sr. DelGenio commandeers a veritable army of volunteers – over 700 – who are inspired by
her selfless love of the poor; additionally, she has obtained help from the Sisters of St. Casimir for
assistance and housing, and has reached out to Holy Cross Hospital for laundry services, as well as to
doctors who are willing to work pro bono for her cause; and
WHEREAS, in an profound way, Sr. DelGenio feels compelled by the Gospel challenge to feed the
hungry and minister to the poor; and yet, Sr. DelGenio was trained as an addictions counselor, and her
love is a tough love; she realizes that people must be able to do for themselves if they are to survive; and
WHEREAS, in addition to helping with shelter/housing placement and employment, PADS offers the
following services on-site and through off-site referrals: Evening Warming Center from October through
April; Daytime Cooling Center from May through September; nutritious, hot meals in winter; bag lunches
year round; shower facilities; change of clothing; haircuts; medical care; mental health care; rehab; eye
glasses; cost-free prescription drugs; and referrals to agencies to meet additional needs; and

1393

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, Sr. DelGenio, in formulating and leading this holistic social program for the past sixteen
years, has touched, helped, provided community for, and healed thousands of God’s children.

Board of Commissioners, do hereby express my deep gratitude to Sr. Therese DelGenio for her ardent
sense of mission, and do hereby commend her for all of the inspired work she has accomplished on behalf
of the residents of Cook County.

09-R-245

THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Thursday, May 7, 2009 is the “National Day of Prayer” in the United States of America;
and
WHEREAS, on this day people of all faiths and spiritual practices are asked to pray for our Nation and
its leaders; and
WHEREAS, created by a joint resolution of the United States Congress and signed into law by Harry S.
Truman in 1952, the “National Day of Prayer” was originally a floating day; in 1988 President Ronald
Reagan amended the law to permanently set the date of the “National Day of Prayer” as the first Thursday
in every May; and
WHEREAS, the “National Day of Prayer” has earlier historical antecedents; the first call to prayer was in
1775, when the Continental Congress asked the Colonies to pray for wisdom in founding a nation; later
during the Undeclared War with France, President John Adams declared May 9, 1799 as “a day of solemn
humiliation, fasting and prayer,” during which citizens of all faiths were asked to pray “that our Country
may be protected from all dangers which threaten it”; and President Abraham Lincoln issued a
Proclamation in 1863 declaring a day of “humiliation, fasting and prayer”; and
WHEREAS, last year local, state and federal observances were held from sunrise in Maine to sunset in
Hawaii, uniting people from all socioeconomic, political and ethnic backgrounds; and

1394

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, on this day, our Nation’s diversity of religious and spiritual practice is embraced and
celebrated.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that Thursday, May 7, 2009, will be known as the
“National Day of Prayer” in Cook County, and on that day people of all faiths and spiritual practices are
urged to come together in prayer for our Nation and its leaders.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

Co-Sponsored by

BRIDGET GAINER, ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, ROBERT B. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
CELEBRATING EL VALOR’S 35TH ANNIVERSARY YEAR
AND ANNUAL DON QUIXOTE DINNER
WHEREAS, El Valor has been celebrating its 35th anniversary this year and will host its annual Don
Quixote Dinner on May 18, 2009; and
WHEREAS, El Valor is a non-profit community-based organization founded in 1973 by the late
Guadalupe A. Reyes; and
WHEREAS, a visionary leader and mother, Mrs. Reyes dreamed of a community in which all members,
including her son with special needs, could live, learn and work; and
WHEREAS, El Valor’s mission is to support and challenge urban families to achieve excellence and
participate fully in community life. Their programs exist to enrich and empower people with disabilities,
the disenfranchised and the underserved; and
WHEREAS, El Valor’s vision is to be the international model for inclusion of people with disabilities, to
be the best in the nation in early childhood and youth enrichment and to become the premier organization
developing Hispanic leadership; and
WHEREAS, the organization has partnered with the White House Initiative on Educational Excellence
for Hispanic Americans and is one of the largest Hispanic serving non-profit organizations in the United
States; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Vincent Allocco has been the President and Executive Director of El Valor for over 20
years having arrived at El Valor in 1979 to join others who shared his dream of excellence and inclusion
for all children and families including people with disabilities; and

1399

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, El Valor has experienced remarkable growth and success under the leadership and direction
of Dr. Allocco. During this time, El Valor has completed two capital campaigns that resulted in the
construction of two state-of-the-art children and family centers. The Guadalupe Reyes Children & Family
Center is located at the heart of Chicago's Pilsen community, and the Rey Gonzalez Children & Family
Center is located in South Chicago; and
WHEREAS, a third Children and Family Center is underway; El Valor is at the end of a capital
campaign that will bring the Carlos Cantu Children & Family Center into the neighborhood of Little
Village/South Lawndale; and
WHEREAS, this year’s Don Quixote Dinner will honor Mr. John T. Hooker with the Guadalupe A.
Reyes Founder’s Award for his commitment to improving the quality of life for those less fortunate as
well as fifty El Valor participants who have won medals at the Special Olympics.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
wholeheartedly congratulates El Valor for their many accomplishments during this, their 35th
Anniversary year; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners does hereby thank Dr. Vincent
Allocco and El Valor for their many years of dedicated service and outstanding contributions to the
Community; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to Dr. Allocco on
behalf of El Valor to commemorate this resplendent occasion.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
