09-R-250
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, President Harry S. Truman led the effort to establish a single holiday for citizens to come
together and thank our military members for their patriotic service in support of our Country; and

1400

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, On August 31, 1949, Secretary of Defense Louis Johnson announced the creation of an
Armed Forces Day to replace the separate Army, Navy, Marine Corps and Air Force Days that were then
in existence; this single-day celebration stemmed from the unification of the Armed Forces under the
Department of Defense; the theme for the first Armed Forces Day was "Teamed for Defense"; and
WHEREAS, Armed Forces Day is different from Memorial Day and Veterans Day; Memorial Day is for
remembering those who died in uniform, those who made the ultimate sacrifice for their country;
Veterans Day is for paying tribute to all of those who have ever worn a military uniform in service of our
country, past and present; and
WHEREAS, Armed Forces Day recognizes the men and women of the Armed Forces throughout the
world, including the young adults who have just joined the military and face the real possibility of going
off to war, instead of to college; right now they are in basic training at Lackland Air Force Base in San
Antonio, Texas; at Fort Dix, New Jersey; at Parris Island, South Carolina; at the Navy's Great Lakes
facility in Illinois; or at one of the other basic training sites the services operate; and
WHEREAS, Armed Forces Day is an occasion to remember those who are now faced with making the
tough decision as to whether to continue to serve their Country; they are weighing the demands that
continued military service brings, whether they are active duty or one of our Citizen Airmen or Citizen
Soldiers who serve in the Reserves or National Guard; and
WHEREAS, Americans throughout this great Nation set aside Armed Forces Day for special
remembrance of the men and women who are serving to protect our freedom; and
WHEREAS, on this special day, our hearts and thoughts turn to those who serve their Country, and to the
sacrifices and hardships they endure; on this special day they earn honor from a grateful Nation.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that I, Todd H. Stroger, President of the Cook County
Board of Commissioners, do hereby recognize May 16, 2009 as Armed Forces Day, and do ask that on
this day all citizens express their gratitude to the members of our esteemed Armed Forces.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

09-R-252
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN P. DALEY, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
AND TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE WILLIAM M. BEAVERS, JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL,
EARLEAN COLLINS, BRIDGET GAINER, ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN,
GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, in 1858, a farmer named John Simpson established his homestead in an oak savannah along
a route known today as 95th Street; and
WHEREAS, the area was soon known as Black Oaks Grove for its namesake trees, and the fertile soil
and abundant resources quickly attracted more farmers to the growing community; and
WHEREAS, in 1879, the Wabash Railroad laid tracks through the community, and a new train station
was constructed and given the name Oak Lawn Depot; and

1403

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, in 1909, the Village of Oak Lawn was first incorporated as a recognized municipality in the
State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the new village experienced rapid population growth, from 500 residents in 1920, to 9,000
by 1950, and 27,000 by the 1960’s; and
WHEREAS, a devastating tornado that caused 13 fatalities in April of 1967 caused only a temporary halt
to Oak Lawn’s growth, as the community demonstrated its true spirit by pulling together and quickly rebuilding; and
WHEREAS, the Village of Oak Lawn today is an economically thriving and culturally diverse
community, with a highly rated police and fire department, outstanding park programs, a renowned
children’s museum, and easy access to transportation; and
WHEREAS, Oak Lawn is home to 57,000 citizens, a thriving commercial district, and one of the
region’s largest hospitals, Advocate Christ Hospital; and
WHEREAS, from its humble origins among the black oak trees, Oak Lawn today is a jewel among the
Southwest Suburbs, with an unsurpassed quality of life for its residents, who know their community as an
outstanding place to live, work, and raise a family.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that the
Board does hereby commemorate the Centennial Anniversary of the date that Oak Lawn was incorporated
as a Village, and offers it greetings to all who will gather for a gala celebration at the Oak Lawn Hilton on
May 16th, 2009; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body, and a suitable copy of same be tendered by the Commissioners of Cook County to The Honorable
Dave Heilmann, Village President, that this historic milestone in the proud history of Oak Lawn be duly
recognized.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, Liza McElroy is stepping down as Director of Parks and Recreation of the Winnetka Park
District after 28 years of service, the last 8 of which were in her current position; and
WHEREAS, Liza McElroy has earned a state-wide reputation as a dedicated parks and recreation
supervisor, and has developed quality programs and events for the Winnetka Park District, including the
annual Fourth of July celebration and fireworks extravaganza; and
WHEREAS, Liza McElroy helped the district build a new administration center, updated the district’s
strategic plan, and built a new paddle tennis facility; and
WHEREAS, Liza McElroy guided the district through the construction of a new service center,
implementing an intergovernmental agreement with the Village of Winnetka to secure a site on the
Village’s landfill and secured a $100,000 grant to study LEED certification for the facility; and
WHEREAS, Liza McElroy and the Winnetka Park District are active supporters of the North Suburban
Special Recreation Association, which provides recreation opportunities for children with special needs;
and
WHEREAS, Liza McElroy has been honored numerous times, including receiving the Robert Artz
Award from the Illinois Park and Recreation Association; the Professional Excellence Award from the
National Recreation and Park Association; and has been named Honored Professional by the Illinois
Association of Park Districts; and
WHEREAS, Liza McElroy is moving on to become the Executive Director of the Park District of
Highland Park.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does offer
its congratulations to Liza McElroy on her accomplishment as Director of the Winnetka Park District and
its thanks for her dedication to improving the lives and community and children of Winnetka; and

IN MEMORY OF ALBERT PICK, III
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III passed away on April 16, 2009; and
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III was a successful investment executive and generous philanthropist; and
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III was born in Evanston in 1934, graduated from Highland Park High School
and Michigan State University, with a degree in economics; and
WHEREAS, upon graduation, Albert Pick, III worked for Albert Pick Hotels Corp., the business started
by his father; and
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III left the family business and entered the stock brokerage and investment
business, heading FGE Industries in Chicago and serving as vice president of Weir Machine and Foundry
Co.; and
WHEREAS, in 1973, Governor Dan Walker named Albert Pick, III to be the state’s commissioner of
savings and loan associations; and
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III worked for many years as an executive with Chicago Corp., later bought by
ABN-AMRO, where he retired as vice president; and
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III was greatly involved in philanthropic organizations, including serving as a
director of the Albert Pick, Jr. Fund, which supported many Chicago-area charities, health and education
groups and arts institutions, including the Adler Planetarium, the Chicago Children’s Choir, the Greater
Chicago Food Depository, the Joffrey Ballet and the Museum of Science and Industry; and
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III was a strong supporter of the Notebaert Nature Museum, where he was a
past president and board member; and
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III was a former president of the Union League Club of Chicago; and

1409

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III is survived by his wife, Kay Levi Pick; his two sons, Thomas F. Pick and
Benjamin Pomeranz; two daughters, Janet Karr and Lisa Nurzia; and nine grandchildren; and
WHEREAS, Albert Pick, III will be deeply missed and forever treasured by all who knew him.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friends of Albert Pick,
III and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Albert
Pick, III so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

09-R-258
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT, WILLIAM M. BEAVERS,
JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
BRIDGET GAINER, ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY,
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER, PETER N. SILVESTRI,
DEBORAH SIMS AND ROBERT B. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN MEMORY OF JUDGE JAMES B. MORAN
WHEREAS, Judge James B. Moran, who served for three decades on the U.S. District Court for the
Northern District of Illinois, died April 21, 2009, following a long illness; and
WHEREAS, Judge Moran was born in Evanston and grew up in Escanaba, Michigan; and
WHEREAS, Judge Moran earned his Bachelor of Arts degree from the University of Michigan in 1952
before entering the U.S. Army; and
WHEREAS, following two years of military service, including service in Korea, Judge Moran enrolled
in Harvard Law School and graduated magna cum laude with his Juris Doctorate degree in 1957; and
WHEREAS, following law school, Judge Moran clerked for Judge J. Edward Lumbard of the 2nd Circuit
from 1957 to 1958; and
WHEREAS, in 1958, Judge Moran joined the firm then called Bell, Boyd, Marshall & Lloyd, which later
became Bell, Boyd, Lloyd, Haddad & Burns in Chicago; and
WHEREAS, Judge Moran’s law practice, first as an associate and then as a partner, focused on
commercial litigation, which was often tried in federal courts; and
WHEREAS, Judge Moran, a committed public servant and independent Democrat, served as a Member
of the Illinois House of Representatives from 1965-67, as an Evanston City Councilman from 1971 to
1974 and served as acting general counsel of the U.S. Senate Ethics Committee in 1977; and
WHEREAS, Judge Moran was appointed to serve on the federal trial bench by President Jimmy Carter in
1979, and served as the District Court’s chief judge from 1990 until attaining senior status in 1995; and
WHEREAS, Judge Moran, a member of numerous bar associations and respected legal organizations,
was universally praised and appreciated by colleagues and attorneys for his outstanding legal ability,
scrupulous fairness, patient and friendly temperament, and overall excellence as a jurist; and

1412

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, Judge Moran cared greatly for his fellow men and women and served as a longtime director
of the Gateway Foundation, Inc., devoted to assisting thousands of individuals struggling with drug
addiction, and the Woodlawn Community Development Corporation; and
WHEREAS, Judge Moran, a loving husband and father, is survived by his wife, Janet P. Remen, one
son, three daughters and nine stepchildren; and
WHEREAS, Judge Moran will be deeply missed by all who knew him. His friend and colleague, U.S.
District Chief Judge James F. Holderman, remembered, Judge Moran as a “person who loved people,
loved lawyers, loved his family and loved being a judge,” and
WHEREAS, the residents of Cook County owe a debt of gratitude to Judge Moran for his noble public
service and commitment to justice.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friends of Judge
James B. Moran and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Judge
James B. Moran so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

DEBORAH SIMS AND ROBERT B. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

1413

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
HONORING ALLEN “BO” PRICE
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price passed away on May 1, 2009; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price was a veteran of World War II, a community leader and inspiration to
countless young people whose lives he touched; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price was born in Evanston on July 1, 1922, to Squire and Gertrude Price; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price graduated from Foster School in Evanston before attending Washburn
Trade Institute in Chicago; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price was drafted into the United States Army after the bombing of Pearl
Harbor and inducted at Fort Sheridan, later receiving training at Fort Custer in Michigan and Fort Sam
Houston in San Antonio; and
WHEREAS, although he was trained to be a quartermaster, after the invasion of France, Allen “Bo”
Price saw combat action and fought in Belgium and the Battle of the Bulge from December 16, 1944 to
January 25, 1945; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price was wounded by shrapnel but later returned to the front lines; and
WHEREAS, upon completion of World War II, Allen “Bo” Price was discharged from the Army and
returned to Evanston; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price was a founding member of the Snell Post of Veterans of Foreign Wars
(VFW), named after the first Evanstonian killed in World War II; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price captained the VFW Drill Team, which quickly became recognized for
their expertise, performing at halftime for many Chicago sporting events, including Chicago Cardinals
and Harlem Globetrotters games; and
WHEREAS, in 1978, Allen “Bo” Price founded the Pride of Evanston Drum and Bugle Corps, which
instilled in young people the discipline and dedication needed to succeed in the world; and
WHEREAS, the Pride of Evanston Drum and Bugle Corps integrated the Evanston 4th of July Parade
and was the first black championship drill team in Illinois; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price became a community resource for young parents, holding seminars and
workshops for teen parents that stressed the importance of the formative years in child development; and
WHEREAS, on January 12, 1998, the City of Evanston honored Allen “Bo” Price with an Honorary
Street Name Designation on Foster Avenue in front of Family Focus/Our Place and the FleetwoodJourdain Community Center, commemorating the contributions that he made to the community and all the
young people he met; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price organized and hosted the City of Evanston’s ceremonies honoring
Memorial Day and Veterans’ Day; and
WHEREAS, Allen “Bo” Price will be deeply missed and forever treasured by all who knew him.

1414

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friends of Allen “Bo”
Price and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Allen
“Bo” Price so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of May 2009.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

300251

STATE’S ATTORNEY, Anita Alvarez, submitting communication advising the County of
the Agreed Order Appointing a Transitional Administrator regarding Jimmy Doe v. County
of Cook, USDC No. 99-C-3945. This class action litigation was originally brought in 1999
and has subsequently involved the entry of a Memorandum of Agreement (MOA) between
the parties that was approved by the District Court in December 2002 and the entry of an
Agreed Supplemental Order approved by the Court on May 18, 2006. This petition was
resolved by the entry of an Agreed Order Appointing a Transitional Administrator (TA) by
the District Court on August 14, 2007. The Board of Commissioners agreed to the entry of
the subject order during its meeting of July 31, 2007.
On June 18, 2008, the District Court entered an order amending this portion of the TA Order
permitting the Transitional Administrator to maintain the OTA funds in a separate account to
pay reasonable costs and expenses of the staff of the OTA. The OTA account was first
funded at $800,000.00 on July 22, 2008 and the District Court entered an order for additional
funds of $500,000.00 on December 18, 2008.
The Transitional Administrator has now presented invoice payment records evidencing
payments and a balance in the account as of February 27, 2009 in the amount of $329,388.17
which has been reviewed and accepted by the Cook County State’s Attorney’s Office. The
TA has requested the District Court to enter an order providing for an additional
disbursement of $500,000.00 into the OTA account which was approved by the Court on
April 18, 2009.
Upon approval, the Cook County Comptroller will transfer $500,000.00 from the SelfInsurance Fund to an account managed by the Transitional Administrator account in
accordance with the terms of the aforementioned court order.
COMMISSIONER PERAICA VOTED NO ON THE ABOVE ITEM.

300042

of Cook County sustained accidental injuries on November 17, 2006. The Petitioner was

298603

ORDINANCE ADOPTING GUIDELINES FOR THE EXPENDITURE AND
REIMBURSEMENT OF CONTINGENCY FUNDS FOR COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
AND STAFF (PROPOSED ORDINANCE). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
Commissioner Peter N. Silvestri and (former) Commissioner Mike Quigley; Co-Sponsored
by Forrest Claypool, John P. Daley, Elizabeth “Liz” Doody Gorman, Gregg Goslin, Anthony
J. Peraica, Timothy O. Schneider and Larry Suffredin, County Commissioners.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE ADOPTING GUIDELINES FOR THE
EXPENDITURE AND REIMBURSEMENT OF CONTINGENCY FUNDS
FOR COUNTY COMMISSIONERS AND STAFF
WHEREAS, the annual budget for the government of Cook County includes
contingency funds for each Commissioner’s office; and
WHEREAS, the contingency fund is appropriated to provide for expenses incurred in the
normal and customary operation of each Commissioner’s office and for the
reimbursement of expenses associated with the normal and customary duties of each
office; and
WHEREAS, the contingency fund is provided to each Commissioner’s office to assist
the Commissioner and his or her staff in the performance of their duties.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners, that Chapter 34 Finance, Article II, Section 34-40 of the Cook County
Code is hereby enacted as follows:
Sec. 34-40.

Use of contingency funds by Commissioners and staff (018-890).

(a)

Contingency funds may be provided to assist Commissioners and
members of their staffs in the execution of official duties.

(b)

The following guidelines shall apply to the expenditure and
reimbursement of contingency funds by each Commissioner’s office:
(1)

Contingency funds shall be expended for:
a.

Office supplies, utilities, or materials;

b.

Costs relating to attendance at meetings and events,
including meals, in the performance of official duties;

c.

Travel and transportation expenses for county functions,
meetings and duties. Such expenses may include
reimbursement for automobile usage;

1461

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009

(2)

d.

Educational programs related to government, finance, or
other topics generally associated with the functions of
county government;

e.

Newspapers, journals, magazines, or books related to
official duties;

f.

Other information or research materials;

g.

Membership fees for non-profit, community, or civic
organizations;

h.

Attendance at civic, social, fraternal, and other events
sponsored by community groups and associations,
including religious and charitable events, as long as such
expenses for attendance are for attendance at such events
and not for the general promotion of any particular
religious, philanthropic, or charitable mission or
objective;

i.

Enhancement of any other budgetary appropriation
within the budget of the office of the Commissioner;

j.

Expenses incurred by staff of the Commissioner, as
approved by the Commissioner, within these guidelines;

k.

Costs directly related to the provision of constituent
services.

Funds shall not be utilized for political activities, including, but
not limited to:
a.

Travel or transportation expenses to political or
fundraising events;

b.

The printing, publishing, or mailing of materials for
political or fundraising events;

c.

Donations to campaign funds.

(3)

Contingency funds shall not be expended for or accepted as
additional income;

(4)

Within 30 days of the end of each quarter of the County’s fiscal
year, each Commissioner shall submit an expenditure report
detailing the expenses incurred by his or her office during that
quarter to the Secretary to the Board of Commissioners,
supported by:

1462

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
a.

Mileage logs and fuel receipts;

b.

Copies of travel documents;

c.

Copies of cancelled checks;

d.

Course descriptions for qualified educational programs;

e.

Receipts for or any other records related to expenses
specified in this Section.

(5)

The Secretary to the Board of Commissioners shall post the
expenditure reports described in subsection (b)(4) to a publicly
accessible web page within 15 days of receipt.

(6)

Monies expended from the contingency fund found not to be in
compliance with the above guidelines shall be returned to Cook
County.

Effective date: This Ordinance shall be effective upon adoption.
* Referred to the Committee on Finance on 02/04/09.
** Deferred 03/17/09 and 04/01/09.

WHEREAS, the annual budget for the government of Cook County includes

WHEREAS, the contingency fund is appropriated to provide for expenses incurred in the

office; and

WHEREAS, the contingency fund is provided to each Commissioner’s office to assist
the Commissioner and his or her staff in the performance of their his or her duties.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners, that Chapter 34 Finance, Article II, Section 34-40 of the Cook County
Code is hereby enacted as follows:
Sec. 34-40.

Use of contingency funds by Commissioners and staff (018-890).

(a)
Contingency funds may be provided to assist Commissioners and
members of their staffs in the execution of official duties.
(b)
The following guidelines shall apply to the expenditure and
reimbursement of contingency funds by each Commissioner’s office:
(1)

Contingency funds shall be expended for:
a.

Office supplies, utilities, or materials;

b. a.

Costs relating to attendance at meetings and events,
including meals, in the performance of official duties;

c. b.

Travel and transportation expenses for county functions,
meetings and duties. Such expenses may include
reimbursement for automobile usage;

d. c.

Educational programs related to government, finance, or
other topics generally associated with the functions of
county government;

e. d.

Newspapers, journals, magazines, or books related to
official duties;

f.

Other information or research materials;

g. e.

Membership fees for non-profit, community, or civic
organizations;

h. f.

Attendance at civic, social, fraternal, and other events
sponsored by community groups and associations,
including religious and charitable events, as long as such
expenses for attendance are for attendance at such events
and not for the general promotion of any particular
religious, philanthropic, or charitable mission or
objective;

i.

Enhancement of any other budgetary appropriation
within the budget of the office of the Commissioner;

j.

Expenses incurred by staff of the Commissioner, as
approved by the Commissioner, within these guidelines;

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
k. g.

(2)

Costs directly related to the provision of constituent
services.

a.

Travel or transportation expenses to political or

b.

The printing, publishing, or mailing of materials for
political or fundraising events;

c.

Donations to campaign funds.

(3)

Contingency funds shall not be expended for or accepted as
additional income;

(4)

Within 30 days of the end of each quarter of the County’s fiscal
year, each Commissioner shall submit an expenditure report
detailing the expenses incurred by his or her office during that
quarter to the Secretary to the Board of Commissioners,
supported by:
a.

Mileage logs, and fuel receipts, and proof of payment for
financing costs associated with a vehicle used in the
performance of official duties;

b.

Copies of travel documents;

c.

Copies of cancelled checks;

d.

Course descriptions for qualified educational programs;

e.

Receipts for or any other records related to expenses
specified in this Section.

The Director of the Cook County Board of Ethics shall
determine compliance with this section.

accessible web page within 15 days of receipt.

(6 7)

Monies expended from the contingency fund found not to be in
compliance with the above guidelines shall be returned to Cook
County.

Effective date: This Ordinance shall be effective upon adoption.

Commissioner’s office; and

1466

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, the contingency fund is appropriated to provide for expenses incurred in the normal and

with the normal and customary duties of each office; and
WHEREAS, the contingency fund is provided to each Commissioner’s office to assist the Commissioner
and his or her staff in the performance of their his or her duties.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners, that Chapter
34 Finance, Article II, Section 34-40 of the Cook County Code is hereby enacted as follows:
Sec. 34-40.

Use of contingency funds by Commissioners and staff (018-890).

(a)
Contingency funds may be provided to assist Commissioners and members of their staffs
in the execution of official duties.
(b)
The following guidelines shall apply to the expenditure and reimbursement of
contingency funds by each Commissioner’s office:
(1)

Contingency funds shall be expended for:
a.

Office supplies, utilities, or materials;

b. a.

Costs relating to attendance at meetings and events, including meals, in the
performance of official duties;

c. b.

Travel and transportation expenses for county functions, meetings and duties.
Such expenses may include reimbursement for automobile usage;

d. c.

Educational programs related to government, finance, or other topics generally
associated with the functions of county government;

e. d.

Newspapers, journals, magazines, or books related to official duties;

f.

Other information or research materials;

g. e.

Membership fees for non-profit, community, or civic organizations;

h. f.

Attendance at civic, social, fraternal, and other events sponsored by community
groups and associations, including religious and charitable events, as long as
such expenses for attendance are for attendance at such events and not for the
general promotion of any particular religious, philanthropic, or charitable mission
or objective;

i.

Enhancement of any other budgetary appropriation within the budget of
the office of the Commissioner;

j.

Expenses incurred by staff of the Commissioner, as approved by the
Commissioner, within these guidelines;

k. g.

Costs directly related to the provision of constituent services.

1467

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
(2)

Funds shall not be utilized for political activities, including, but not limited to:
a.

Travel or transportation expenses to political or fundraising events;

b.

The printing, publishing, or mailing of materials for political or fundraising
events;

c.

Donations to campaign funds.

(3)

Contingency funds shall not be expended for or accepted as additional income;

(4)

Within 30 days of the end of each quarter of the County’s fiscal year, each Commissioner
shall submit an expenditure report detailing the expenses incurred by his or her office
during that quarter to the Secretary to the Board of Commissioners, supported by:

(5)

a.

Mileage logs, and fuel receipts; and proof of payment for financing costs
associated with a vehicle used in performance of official duties;

b.

Copies of travel documents;

c.

Copies of cancelled checks;

d.

Course descriptions for qualified educational programs;

e.

Receipts for or any other records related to expenses specified in this Section.

The Director of the Cook County Board of Ethics shall determine compliance with this
section.

(5) (6) The Secretary to the Board of Commissioners shall post the expenditure reports described
in subsection (b)(4) to a publicly accessible web page within 15 days of receipt.
(6) (7) Monies expended from the contingency fund found not to be in compliance with the
above guidelines shall be returned to Cook County.

Your Subcommittee has considered the following item and, upon adoption of this report, the
recommendation is follows:
298816

CLERK OF THE CIRCUIT COURT, Dorothy Brown, transmitting a Communication, dated
February 9, 2009:
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with P. NEILL
PETRONELLA, Chicago, Illinois, for professional services as a labor relations consultant.
Reason:

P. Neill Petronella was selected through the Request For Qualifications (RFQ)
process. Three vendors submitted responses to the RFQ. The vendor that was
selected met all requirements under the RFQ process, had extensive knowledge
and experience in employment and labor relations, and was the lowest cost.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $199,500.00 $182,000.00. (FY 2009: $170,620.00 $153,120.00;
and FY 2010: $28,880.00). Contract period: March 1, 2009 April 1, 2009 through February
28, 2010. (335-261 Account). Requisition No. 93350014.
*Referred to the Finance Committee on February 18, 2009.
* *Referred to the Litigation Subcommittee on March 4, 2009.

Communication No. 298816, as amended. The motion carried.

OFFICE OF THE COUNTY AUDITOR

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
PURCHASE ORDER ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 15, 2009 from
DAVID ORR, County Clerk
by
CLEM BALANOFF, Deputy Clerk
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to increase by $3,205.00, Purchase Order No. 165381000-OP with Gary M. Rycyzyn Consulting, Tinley Park, Illinois, for ballot management consulting
services.
Original Purchase Order amount issued 01-15-09:
Increase requested:
Adjusted amount:
Reason:

$20,000.00
3,250.00
$23,250.00

Gary Rycyzyn’s help preparing the Cook County ballots exceeded the time and dollar value
allocated under this purchase order. The consolidated election in Cook County is one of the
most complex elections in the country. This year, the job of putting together the ballot was
made more difficult by late ballot changes, some occurring after early voting had started. Mr.
Rycyzyn worked for the Cook County Clerk's Office for 30 years and served as the Director
of Elections for twelve years. His knowledge of the complexities of the voting districts, data,
and experience managing the certification of over 3,100 candidates and the layout of over 800
ballot styles was invaluable. The expiration date of the purchase order was April 8, 2009.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $3,250.00. (524-260 Account).
Sufficient funds are available in the County Clerk's Election Division Fund.
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to increase the requested Purchase Order. The motion carried unanimously.

JUDICIARY
ILLINOIS NOT-FOR-PROFIT DISPUTE RESOLUTION ACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 10, 2009 from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
respectfully request that, pursuant to General Administrative Order 2009-01, the Cook County Board of
Commissioners approve the disbursement of funds totaling $200,000.00 from the Not-For-Profit Dispute
Resolution Fund, County Fund 531, to the Center for Conflict Resolution (Center). The Center was the
only qualifying applicant for these funds in 2008.

1498

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
The disbursement will have no fiscal impact on Cook County since, by statute, fees from civil filings are
collected solely for this purpose. There are sufficient funds available in 531-818 Account,
Reimbursement to Designated Fund, for this purpose.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $200,000.00. (531-818 Account).
IN THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS
GENERAL ADMINISTRATIVE ORDER NO. 2009-01
SUBJECT: ILLINOIS NOT-FOR-PROFIT DISPUTE RESOLUTION ACT
Pursuant to the Illinois Not-For-Profit Dispute Resolution Act (710 ILCS 20/1 et seq.), the Clerk
of the Circuit Court of Cook County has collected fees from civil filings for disbursement to the Dispute
Resolution Centers which qualify under said Act and General Order 19 of the Circuit Court of Cook
County. Fees available for disbursement from this Fund for the year 2008 total $258,740.00.
Upon review of applications received for funds collected in 2008, the sole qualifying applicant
under the requirements set forth in said Act and General Order 19 of the Circuit Court of Cook County
was found to be the Center for Conflict Resolution. It is eligible for the maximum amount allowable for
disbursement to any Dispute Resolution Center in a given year of $200,000.00.
Pursuant to the Illinois Not-For-Profit Dispute Resolution Act (710 ILCS 20/1 et seq.), any funds
collected but not disbursed in a given year shall be paid in single county judicial circuits to the County
Treasurer for the administration of justice in the judicial circuit. An amount of $58,740.00 remains
collected for the year 2008 but no other Dispute Resolution Center is qualified to receive disbursement of
these funds.
Therefore, it is hereby ordered that the amount of $200,000.00, representing the maximum
amount allowable for disbursement to any Dispute Resolution Center in a given year, shall be disbursed
to the Center for Conflict Resolution.
Further, it hereby ordered that the amount of $58,740.00 representing funds collected under the
Illinois Not-For-Profit Dispute Resolution Act for 2008 but not disbursed shall be paid to the Treasurer of
Cook County for the administration of justice in the Circuit Court of Cook County.
_________________________
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the request of the Chief Judge of
the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

JUVENILE PROBATION AND COURT SERVICES DEPARTMENT
CONTRACT ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 2, 2009 from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to increase by $1,341,583.00 and extend for nine (9)
months, Contract No. 05-41-280 with Heartland Human Care Services, Inc., Chicago, Illinois, to provide
short term housing and living assistance for minors charged with delinquency petitions in juvenile court.

1499

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
These services are provided to minors ages 10 to 17 who have been referred from the Juvenile Justice
Division to staff-secure shelters by the court's Juvenile Probation and Court Services Department. These
minors are either eligible for admission to the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center (JTDC) and qualify
for placement with Heartland under the Juvenile Detention Alternatives Program or are residents of the
JTDC who have been released from detention by judicial order and whose parents or guardians will not or
cannot secure their release. Contract services include housing and meals, living skills instruction,
counseling, recreation, transportation, 24-hour supervision, medical and psychiatric services, and referrals
to community resources as needed. There are two (2) staff-secure shelters: the Manuel Saura Center for
Boys, 2732 North Kedzie, in Chicago's Logan Square community and the Morse Home for Girls, 1628
West Morse Avenue, in Chicago's Rogers Park community.

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT
PROPOSED RESOLUTIONS
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 21, 2009 from
MAURICE S. JONES, Director, Department of Planning and Development
respectfully submitting the following resolution regarding Lanert Properties, LLC's application for a
Class 8 property tax incentive.
Lanert Properties, LLC requests approval of the tax incentive based on Special Circumstances,
abandonment, under the Class 8 Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the company can
complete its application to the Assessor of Cook County.

1502

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
Lanert Properties, LLC's application for a Class 8, and a Department of Planning and Development staff
report have been submitted for your information.
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
TODD H. STROGER, President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 8 that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for a facility; and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from Lanert
Properties, LLC, Resolution No. 85 of the Village of Lansing for an abandoned facility located at 3720
Ridge Road, Lansing, Cook County, Illinois, County Board District #6, Property Index Numbers 30-32402-019-0000, 30-32-402-020-0000, 30-32-402-021-0000, 30-32-402-022-0000, 30-32-402-029-0000,
and 30-32-402-030-0000; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has defined "abandoned property" as a building and other structures that, after
having been vacant and unused for at least 24 months, are purchased for value by a purchaser in whom
the seller has no direct financial interest; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has defined an exception to this abandoned property definition shall be, if
the municipality or the Board of Commissioners, finds that special circumstances justify finding that the
property is "abandoned" for purpose of Class 8; and
WHEREAS, in the case of abandonment of less than 24 months and purchase for value, by a purchaser in
whom the seller has no direct financial interest the County may determine that special circumstances
justify finding the property is deemed "abandoned"; and
WHEREAS, Class 8 requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of qualifying
abandonment in cases where the facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive months upon
purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for one month at the time of purchase and currently vacant to date, and that special circumstances are
present; and the applicant estimates that eighty new full time jobs and twenty part time jobs will be
created, along with an estimated one hundred construction jobs will be created; and
WHEREAS, the Village of Lansing cites the special circumstances as the property is in need of
revitalization and that without a Class 8 designation the development of this area cannot be accomplished.
There is substantial deterioration of said property including an outdated and insufficient HVAC system; a
worn and inadequate roof which will require replacement; and electrical and plumbing systems which are
incapable of providing adequate service to the intended use of the premises as a restaurant; all of which
will require the new owner to expend approximately $800,000.00 to $950,000.00 to renovate the
property.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners validate the property
located at 3720 Ridge Road, Lansing, Illinois, Cook County, Illinois, is deemed "abandoned" with special
circumstances under the Class 8; and

1503

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.

Transmitting a Communication, dated April 21, 2009 from
MAURICE S. JONES, Director, Department of Planning and Development
respectfully submitting the following resolution regarding TKD Holdings, LLC's application for a Class 8
property tax incentive.
TKD Holdings, LLC requests approval of the tax incentive based on Special Circumstances,
abandonment, under the Class 8 Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the company can
complete its application to the Assessor of Cook County.
TKD Holdings, LLC's application for a Class 8, and a Department of Planning and Development staff
report have been submitted for your information.
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
TODD H. STROGER, President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 8 that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for a facility; and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from TKD
Holdings, LLC, Resolution from the Village of South Holland for an abandoned facility located at 16525
Van Dam Road, South Holland, Cook County, Illinois, County Board District #6, Property Index Number
29-23-201-014-0000; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has defined abandoned property as buildings and other structures that, after
having been vacant and unused for at least 24 months, are purchased for value by a purchaser in whom
the seller has no direct financial interest; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has defined an exception to this abandoned property definition shall be, if
the municipality or the Board of Commissioners, finds that special circumstances justify finding that the
property is abandoned for purpose of Class 8; and
WHEREAS, in the case of abandonment of less than 24 months and purchase for value, by a purchaser in
whom the seller has no direct financial interest the County may determine that special circumstances
justify finding the property is deemed abandoned; and
WHEREAS, Class 8 requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of qualifying
abandonment in cases where the facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive months upon
purchase; and

1504

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for 12 months at the time of purchase and vacant to date and that special circumstances are present; and
the applicant estimates that eighty new full time jobs and twenty part time jobs will be created, and an
estimated one hundred construction jobs will be created; and
WHEREAS, the Village of South Holland cites the special circumstances as the Class 8 is necessary for
development to occur and the property is in need of revitalization including the rehabilitation of a 27,000
square foot building, and the property has been vacant for 12 months and has been continuously marketed
but without locating a buyer. The property is subject to the Village of South Holland Sunday Closing
Laws which limit the right of a business or commercial entity to operate a business on Sunday The
building and property are to be purchased for $736,000.00 and the owner plans to invest an additional
$700,000.00 into the property in order to make it useable for the owners business.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners validate the property
located at 16525 Van Dam Road, South Holland, Cook County, Illinois, is deemed abandoned with
special circumstances under the Class 8; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.
_________________________
This item was WITHDRAWN at the request of the sponsor.

1505

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 6b that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for an industrial facility;
and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from DEC
Investment Group, LLC and Resolution No. 49-08 from the Village of Melrose Park for an abandoned
industrial facility located at 2755 West LeMoyne Street, Melrose Park, Cook County, Illinois, County
Board District #16, Property Index Number 15-04-204-014-0000; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has defined abandoned property as buildings and other structures that, after
having been vacant and unused for at least 24 months, are purchased for value by a purchaser in whom
the seller has no direct financial interest; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has defined an exception to this abandoned property definition shall be, if the
municipality or the Board of Commissioners, finds that special circumstances justify finding that the
property is abandoned for purpose of Class 6b; and
WHEREAS, in the case of abandonment of more than 24 months and no purchase for value by a
disinterested buyer, the County may determine that special circumstances justify finding the property is
deemed abandoned; and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires a resolution by the County Board validating the property is deemed
abandoned for the purposes of Class 6b; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building has been
abandoned and vacant since October 2006 and there has been no purchase for value, and that special
circumstances are present; and
WHEREAS, the re-occupancy will create new jobs, the number to be determined once the property has
been leased and where the Village of Melrose Park cites the special circumstances is necessary for
development to occur including the subject property is an obsolete industrial building that has been vacant
and unused for twenty-four (24) months with characteristics that do no lend the building to modern
manufacturing, warehousing and/or industrial purposes, and which building is in need of significant
rehabilitation, and the applicant owns the building and desires to rehabilitate the subject property,
including repairing the roof and upgrading electricity and utility functions; and
WHEREAS, the applicant acknowledges that it must provide an affidavit to the Assessors' Office
stipulating that it is in compliance with the County Living Wage Ordinance prior to receiving the Class 6b
incentive on the subject property.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners validate the property
located at 2755 West LeMoyne Street, Melrose Park, Cook County, Illinois, is deemed abandoned with
special circumstances under the Class 6b; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009

REAL ESTATE MANAGEMENT DIVISION
TERMINATION OF A PUBLIC WAY LICENSE AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 14, 2009 from
RAYMOND MULDOON, Director, Real Estate Management Division
respectfully requesting termination of the Public Way License Agreement between the County of Cook,
as Grantor, and GSF Energy, LLC, as Grantee, approved by the Cook County Board of Commissioners
on May 7, 2008.
GSF Energy, LLC has requested to terminate this agreement since it has ceased operating its pipeline
located east of Kedzie Avenue along 123rd Street in the City of Blue Island and Village of Alsip. GSF
Energy, LLC has no other facilities within the County public ways.
A field inspection report from the Cook County Highway Department indicates that GSF Energy, LLC has
fulfilled all requirements of the Cook County Highway Department to properly close the pipeline and
restore the public way.
The termination of this license is in accordance with Cook County Code, Chapter 66 Roads and Bridges
Article III Public Way Regulatory Ordinance, approved by the Board of Commissioners on June 19,
2007.
_________________________
Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the request of the Director of the
Real Estate Management Division be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

1519

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
OFFICE OF THE COUNTY TREASURER
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 21, 2009 from
MARIA PAPPAS, Cook County Treasurer
by
MICHAEL J. SHINE, Chief Deputy Treasurer
submitting a proposed Taxing District Debt Disclosure Ordinance that would provide transparency in
government and further the goal of full disclosure to Taxpayers.
Taxpayers are entitled to have readily available to them full disclosure of all debts and liabilities of each
taxing district. With few exceptions, this information is prepared as a matter of course each fiscal year
and would not require additional accounting work from taxing districts.
This proposed ordinance creates a single electronic repository which would allow taxpayers to
electronically access the financial information they need to make informed decisions about the taxing
districts they support. The Treasurer's Office website would house and maintain the electronic
infrastructure where each taxing district would be able to upload their information and make that
information electronically available to taxpayers.
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
TODD H. STROGER, President, FORREST CLAYPOOL, JOHN P. DALEY,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY and ANTHONY J. PERAICA, County Commissioners
Co-Sponsored by
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO and
LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
TAXING DISTRICT DEBT DISCLOSURE ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, Cook County (the “County”) is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article
VII, Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such, may exercise any power and perform any
function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the Office of the Cook County Treasurer (“Treasurer”) issues approximately 1.7 million tax
bills twice yearly; and
WHEREAS, the annual 2nd installment of said tax bills issued by the Treasurer reflect the rates based
upon the final levys of approximately 1,600 taxing districts in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the goal of complete transparency of all financial information pertaining to all Taxing
Districts in Cook County is furthered by the providing of readily available tax information to taxpayers on
the Internet; and

1520

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009
WHEREAS, by virtue of the fact that the Taxpayers of Cook County are paying both the current and
long term debt and liabilities of each such Taxing District, the Taxpayers of Cook County are entitled to
full disclosure of the audited financial statements and financial condition of each taxing district including
but not limited to both the current and long term debt and liabilities of each such Taxing District; and
WHEREAS, the Treasurer has agreed to provide and maintain an electronic repository of the most recent
audited financial statement and financial condition for each taxing district, including but not limited to
both the current and long term debt and liabilities reported by each taxing district pursuant to this
Ordinance; and
WHEREAS, the Treasurer has further agreed to provide on all regularly issued tax bills the web-address
of such electronic repository of the audited financial statements and financial condition of each taxing
district, including but not limited to the current and long term debt and liabilities of Taxing Districts for
which taxes are collected by her Office.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners, that Chapter
2 Administration, Section 2-243 of the Cook County Code is hereby enacted as follows:
Sec. 2-243. Taxing district debt disclosure.
(a) Definitions.
Audited financial statements, current debt, current liabilities, long term debt and long term
liabilities shall have the same meanings as defined by Generally Accepted Accounting Principles, as
promulgated from time to time, by the American Institute of Certified Public Accountants and shall
conform with the accounting principles and auditing standards generally accepted in the United States.
Taxing District shall have the same meaning as defined by 35 ILCS 200/1-150.
(b) Duty of Taxing Districts to disclose all debt. Each Taxing District shall, on or before the last
Tuesday in December, provide to the Office of the Cook County Treasurer, in the electronic format
required by Office of the Cook County Treasurer, such Taxing District’s most recent, full, complete,
unabridged and unedited, audited financial statement (along with all auditor’s notes and comments on
such audited financial statements), including but not limited to the disclosure of any and all actual or
contingent: (i) current debt; (ii) current liabilities; (iii) long term debt; and, (iv) long term liabilities. A
Taxing District, whose audited financial statements are included and/or consolidated in the audited
financial statements of another taxing district, is not required to separately provide the required audited
financial statements in the event said other taxing district is in compliance with the requirements of this
Ordinance.
(c) Duty of Treasurer to make available disclosure of debt. The Office of the Cook County
Treasurer shall:
(1)

Create an electronic repository for the storage of all financial disclosures made by
such taxing districts; and,

(2)

Shall cause to be published on each regularly issued real estate tax bill the website
address which provides electronic access to taxpayers and other interested parties of such
financial disclosures by such taxing districts.

Effective Date: This Ordinance shall take effect upon adoption.

1521

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 5, 2009

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 300316). The motion carried unanimously.
